<code>childNodes</code>. </p> <p>Most browsers return a NodeList object for the method <code>querySelectorAll()</code>.</p> <p>The following code selects all <code><p></code> nodes in a document:</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <div>const myNodeList = document.querySelectorAll("p");</div> <p>The elements in the NodeList can be accessed by an index number.</p> <p>To access the second <p> node you can write:</p> <div>myNodeList[1]</div> <a href="https://www.w3schools.com/js/tryit.asp?filename=tryjs_dom_nodelist" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Try it Yourself »</a> </div> <p><strong>Note:</strong> The index starts at 0.</p> <hr /> <h2>HTML DOM Node List Length</h2> <p>The <code>length</code> property defines the number of nodes in a node list:</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <div>myNodelist.length</div> <a href="https://www.w3schools.com/js/tryit.asp?filename=tryjs_dom_nodelist_length" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Try it Yourself »</a> </div> <p>The <code>length</code> property is useful when you want to loop through the nodes in a node list:</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <p>Change the color of all <p> elements in a node list:</p> <div>const myNodelist = document.querySelectorAll("p"); for (let i = 0; i < myNodelist.length; i++) { myNodelist[i].style.color = "red"; }</div> <a href="https://www.w3schools.com/js/tryit.asp?filename=tryjs_dom_nodelist_loop" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Try it Yourself »</a> </div> <hr /> <hr /> <h2>The Difference Between an HTMLCollection and a NodeList</h2> <p>A <strong>NodeList</strong> and an <strong>HTMLcollection</strong> is very much the same thing. </p> <p>Both are array-like collections (lists) of nodes (elements) extracted from a document. The nodes can be accessed by index numbers. The index starts at 0.</p> <p>Both have a <strong>length</strong> property that returns the number of elements in the list (collection).</p> <p>An HTMLCollection is a collection of <strong>document elements</strong>.</p> <p>A NodeList is a collection of <strong>document nodes</strong> (element nodes, attribute nodes, and text nodes).</p> <p>HTMLCollection items can be accessed by their name, id, or index number.</p> <p>NodeList items can only be accessed by their index number.</p> <p>An HTMLCollection is always a <strong>live</strong> collection. Example: If you add a <li> element to a list in the DOM, the list in the HTMLCollection will also change.</p> <p>A NodeList is most often a <strong>static</strong> collection. Example: If you add a <li> element to a list in the DOM, the list in NodeList will not change.</p> <p>The <code>getElementsByClassName()</code> and <code>getElementsByTagName()</code> methods return a live HTMLCollection.</p> <p>The <code>querySelectorAll()</code> method returns a static NodeList.</p> <p>The <code>childNodes</code> property returns a live NodeList.</p> <hr /> <div> <h2>Not an Array!</h2> <p>A NodeList may look like an array, but it is not.</p> <p>You can loop through a NodeList and refer to its nodes by index.</p> <p>But, you cannot use Array methods like push(), pop(), or join() on a NodeList.</p> </div> <h1>JavaScript Window - The Browser Object Model</h1> <p>The Browser Object Model (BOM) allows JavaScript to "talk to" the browser.</p> <hr /> <h2>The Browser Object Model (BOM)</h2> <p>There are no official standards for the <strong>B</strong>rowser <strong>O</strong>bject <strong>M</strong>odel (BOM).</p> <p>Since modern browsers have implemented (almost) the same methods and properties for JavaScript interactivity, it is often referred to, as methods and properties of the BOM.</p> <hr /> <h2>The Window Object</h2> <p>The <code>window</code> object is supported by all browsers. It represents the browser's window.</p> <p>All global JavaScript objects, functions, and variables automatically become members of the window object.</p> <p>Global variables are properties of the window object.</p> <p>Global functions are methods of the window object.</p> <p>Even the document object (of the HTML DOM) is a property of the window object:</p> <div> <div>window.document.getElementById("header");</div> </div> <p>is the same as:</p> <div> <div>document.getElementById("header");</div> </div> <hr /> <h2>Window Size</h2> <p>Two properties can be used to determine the size of the browser window.</p> <p>Both properties return the sizes in pixels:</p> <ul> <li><code>window.innerHeight</code> - the inner height of the browser window (in pixels) </li> <li><code>window.innerWidth</code> - the inner width of the browser window (in pixels)</li> </ul> <div> <p>The browser window (the browser viewport) is NOT including toolbars and scrollbars.</p> </div> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <div>let w = window.innerWidth; let h = window.innerHeight;</div> <a href="https://www.w3schools.com/js/tryit.asp?filename=tryjs_win_inner" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Try it Yourself »</a> </div> <hr /> <h2>Other Window Methods</h2> <p>Some other methods:</p> <ul> <li><code>window.open()</code> - open a new window</li> <li><code>window.close()</code> - close the current window</li> <li><code>window.moveTo()</code> - move the current window</li> <li><code>window.resizeTo()</code> - resize the current window</li> </ul> <h1>JavaScript Window Screen</h1> <p>The window.screen object contains information about the user's screen.</p> <hr /> <h2>Window Screen</h2> <p>The <code>window.screen</code> object can be written without the window prefix.</p> <p>Properties:</p> <ul> <li><code>screen.width</code></li> <li><code>screen.height</code></li> <li><code>screen.availWidth</code></li> <li><code>screen.availHeight</code></li> <li><code>screen.colorDepth</code></li> <li><code>screen.pixelDepth</code></li> </ul> <hr /> <h2>Window Screen Width</h2> <p>The <code>screen.width</code> property returns the width of the visitor's screen in pixels.</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <p>Display the width of the screen in pixels:</p> <div>document.getElementById("demo").innerHTML = "Screen Width: " + screen.width; </div> <p>Result will be:</p> <div><code>Screen Width: 1366</code></div> <a href="https://www.w3schools.com/js/tryit.asp?filename=tryjs_screen_width" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Try it Yourself »</a> </div> <hr /> <h2>Window Screen Height</h2> <p>The <code>screen.height</code> property returns the height of the visitor's screen in pixels.</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <p>Display the height of the screen in pixels:</p> <div>document.getElementById("demo").innerHTML = "Screen Height: " + screen.height;</div> <p>Result will be:</p> <div><code>Screen Height: 768</code></div> <a href="https://www.w3schools.com/js/tryit.asp?filename=tryjs_screen_height" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Try it Yourself »</a> </div> <hr /> <hr /> <h2>Window Screen Available Width</h2> <p>The <code>screen.availWidth</code> property returns the width of the visitor's screen, in pixels, minus interface features like the Windows Taskbar.</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <p>Display the available width of the screen in pixels:</p> <div>document.getElementById("demo").innerHTML = "Available Screen Width: " + screen.availWidth;</div> <p>Result will be:</p> <div><code>Available Screen Width: 1366</code></div> <a href="https://www.w3schools.com/js/tryit.asp?filename=tryjs_screen_availwidth" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Try it Yourself »</a> </div> <hr /> <h2>Window Screen Available Height</h2> <p>The <code>screen.availHeight</code> property returns the height of the visitor's screen, in pixels, minus interface features like the Windows Taskbar.</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <p>Display the available height of the screen in pixels:</p> <div>document.getElementById("demo").innerHTML = "Available Screen Height: " + screen.availHeight;</div> <p>Result will be:</p> <div><code>Available Screen Height: 736</code></div> <a href="https://www.w3schools.com/js/tryit.asp?filename=tryjs_screen_availheight" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Try it Yourself »</a> </div> <hr /> <h2>Window Screen Color Depth</h2> <p>The <code>screen.colorDepth</code> property returns the number of bits used to display one color.</p> <p>All modern computers use 24 bit or 32 bit hardware for color resolution:</p> <ul> <li>24 bits = 16,777,216 different "True Colors"</li> <li>32 bits = 4,294,967,296 different "Deep Colors"</li> </ul> <p>Older computers used 16 bits: 65,536 different "High Colors" resolution.</p> <p>Very old computers, and old cell phones used 8 bits: 256 different "VGA colors".</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <p>Display the color depth of the screen in bits:</p> <div>document.getElementById("demo").innerHTML = "Screen Color Depth: " + screen.colorDepth;</div> <p>Result will be:</p> <div><code>Screen Color Depth: 24</code></div> <a href="https://www.w3schools.com/js/tryit.asp?filename=tryjs_screen_colorDepth" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Try it Yourself »</a> </div> <div> <p>The #rrggbb (rgb) values used in HTML represents "True Colors" (16,777,216 different colors) </p> </div> <hr /> <h2>Window Screen Pixel Depth</h2> <p>The <code>screen.pixelDepth</code> property returns the pixel depth of the screen.</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <p>Display the pixel depth of the screen in bits:</p> <div>document.getElementById("demo").innerHTML = "Screen Pixel Depth: " + screen.pixelDepth;</div> <p>Result will be:</p> <div><code>Screen Pixel Depth: 24</code></div> <a href="https://www.w3schools.com/js/tryit.asp?filename=tryjs_screen_pixelDepth" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Try it Yourself »</a> </div> <div> <p>For modern computers, Color Depth and Pixel Depth are equal.</p> </div> <h1>JavaScript Window Location</h1> <p>The <code>window.location</code> object can be used to get the current page address (URL) and to redirect the browser to a new page.</p> <hr /> <h2>Window Location</h2> <p>The <code>window.location</code> object can be written without the window prefix.</p> <p>Some examples:</p> <ul> <li><code>window.location.href</code> returns the href (URL) of the current page</li> <li><code>window.location.hostname</code> returns the domain name of the web host</li> <li><code>window.location.pathname</code> returns the path and filename of the current page </li> <li><code>window.location.protocol</code> returns the web protocol used (http: or https:) </li> <li><code>window.location.assign()</code> loads a new document</li> </ul> <hr /> <h2>Window Location Href</h2> <p>The <code>window.location.href</code> property returns the URL of the current page.</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <p>Display the href (URL) of the current page:</p> <div>document.getElementById("demo").innerHTML = "Page location is " + window.location.href;</div> <p>Result is:</p> <div><code>Page location is https://www.w3schools.com/js/js_window_location.asp</code></div> <a href="https://www.w3schools.com/js/tryit.asp?filename=tryjs_loc_href" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Try it Yourself »</a> </div> <hr /> <h2>Window Location Hostname</h2> <p>The <code>window.location.hostname</code> property returns the name of the internet host (of the current page).</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <p>Display the name of the host:</p> <div>document.getElementById("demo").innerHTML = "Page hostname is " + window.location.hostname;</div> <p>Result is:</p> <div><code>Page hostname is www.w3schools.com</code></div> <a href="https://www.w3schools.com/js/tryit.asp?filename=tryjs_loc_host" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Try it Yourself »</a> </div> <hr /> <hr /> <h2>Window Location Pathname</h2> <p>The <code>window.location.pathname</code> property returns the pathname of the current page.</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <p>Display the path name of the current URL:</p> <div>document.getElementById("demo").innerHTML = "Page path is " + window.location.pathname;</div> <p>Result is:</p> <div><code>Page path is /js/js_window_location.asp</code></div> <a href="https://www.w3schools.com/js/tryit.asp?filename=tryjs_loc_pathname" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Try it Yourself »</a> </div> <hr /> <h2>Window Location Protocol</h2> <p>The <code>window.location.protocol</code> property returns the web protocol of the page.</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <p>Display the web protocol:</p> <div>document.getElementById("demo").innerHTML = "Page protocol is " + window.location.protocol;</div> <p>Result is:</p> <div><code>Page protocol is https:</code></div> <a href="https://www.w3schools.com/js/tryit.asp?filename=tryjs_loc_protocol" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Try it Yourself »</a> </div> <hr /> <h2>Window Location Port</h2> <p>The <code>window.location.port</code> property returns the number of the internet host port (of the current page).</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <p>Display the name of the host:</p> <div>document.getElementById("demo").innerHTML = "Port number is " + window.location.port;</div> <p>Result is:</p> <div><code>Port number is</code></div> <a href="https://www.w3schools.com/js/tryit.asp?filename=tryjs_loc_port" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Try it Yourself »</a> </div> <div> <p>Most browsers will not display default port numbers (80 for http and 443 for https)</p> </div> <hr /> <h2>Window Location Assign</h2> <p>The <code>window.location.assign()</code> method loads a new document.</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <p>Load a new document:</p> <xmp> <html> <head> <script> function newDoc() { window.location.assign("https://www.w3schools.com") } </script> </head> <body> <input type="button" value="Load new document" onclick="newDoc()"> </body> </html> </xmp> </div> <h1>JavaScript Window History</h1> <p>The <code>window.history</code> object contains the browsers history.</p> <hr /> <h2>Window History</h2> <p>The <code>window.history</code> object can be written without the window prefix.</p> <p>To protect the privacy of the users, there are limitations to how JavaScript can access this object.</p> <p>Some methods:</p> <ul> <li><code>history.back()</code> - same as clicking back in the browser</li> <li><code>history.forward()</code> - same as clicking forward in the browser</li> </ul> <hr /> <h2>Window History Back</h2> <p>The <code>history.back()</code> method loads the previous URL in the history list.</p> <p>This is the same as clicking the Back button in the browser.</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <p>Create a back button on a page:</p> <xmp> <html> <head> <script> function goBack() { window.history.back() } </script> </head> <body> <input type="button" value="Back" onclick="goBack()"> </body> </html> </xmp> <p>The output of the code above will be:</p> <div><input type="button" value="Back" /></div> </div> <hr /> <hr /> <h2>Window History Forward</h2> <p>The <code>history.forward()</code> method loads the next URL in the history list.</p> <p>This is the same as clicking the Forward button in the browser.</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <p>Create a forward button on a page:</p> <xmp> <html> <head> <script> function goForward() { window.history.forward() } </script> </head> <body> <input type="button" value="Forward" onclick="goForward()"> </body> </html> </xmp> </div> <h1>JavaScript Window Navigator</h1> <p>The <code>window.navigator</code> object contains information about the visitor's browser.</p> <hr /> <h2>Window Navigator</h2> <p>The <code>window.navigator</code> object can be written without the window prefix.</p> <p>Some examples:</p> <ul> <li><code>navigator.cookieEnabled</code></li> <li><code>navigator.appCodeName</code></li> <li><code>navigator.platform</code></li> </ul> <hr /> <h2>Browser Cookies</h2> <p>The <code>cookieEnabled</code> property returns true if cookies are enabled, otherwise false:</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <div> <p id="demo"></p> <script> document.getElementById("demo").innerHTML = "cookiesEnabled is " + navigator.cookieEnabled; </script></div> <a href="https://www.w3schools.com/js/tryit.asp?filename=tryjs_nav_cookieenabled" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Try it Yourself »</a> </div> <hr /> <h2>Browser Application Name</h2> <p>The <code>appName</code> property returns the application name of the browser:</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <div> <p id="demo"></p> <script> document.getElementById("demo").innerHTML = "navigator.appName is " + navigator.appName; </script></div> <a href="https://www.w3schools.com/js/tryit.asp?filename=tryjs_nav_appname" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Try it Yourself »</a> </div> <div> <h2>Warning</h2> <p>This property is removed (deprecated) in the latest web standard.</p> <p>Most browsers (IE11, Chrome, Firefox, Safari) returns <strong>Netscape</strong> as appName.</p> </div> <hr /> <hr /> <h2>Browser Application Code Name</h2> <p>The <code>appCodeName</code> property returns the application code name of the browser: </p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <div> <p id="demo"></p> <script> document.getElementById("demo").innerHTML = "navigator.appCodeName is " + navigator.appCodeName; </script></div> <a href="https://www.w3schools.com/js/tryit.asp?filename=tryjs_nav_appcodename" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Try it Yourself »</a> </div> <div> <h2>Warning</h2> <p>This property is removed (deprecated) in the latest web standard.</p> <p>Most browsers (IE11, Chrome, Firefox, Safari, Opera) returns <strong>Mozilla</strong> as appCodeName.</p> </div> <hr /> <h2>The Browser Engine</h2> <p>The <code>product</code> property returns the product name of the browser engine:</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <div> <p id="demo"></p> <script> document.getElementById("demo").innerHTML = "navigator.product is " + navigator.product; </script></div> <a href="https://www.w3schools.com/js/tryit.asp?filename=tryjs_nav_product" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Try it Yourself »</a> </div> <div> <h2>Warning</h2> <p>This property is removed (deprecated) in the latest web standard.</p> <p>Most browsers returns <strong>Gecko</strong> as product.</p> </div> <hr /> <h2>The Browser Version</h2> <p>The <code>appVersion</code> property returns version information about the browser:</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <div> <p id="demo"></p> <script> document.getElementById("demo").innerHTML = navigator.appVersion; </script></div> <a href="https://www.w3schools.com/js/tryit.asp?filename=tryjs_nav_appversion" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Try it Yourself »</a> </div> <h2>The Browser Agent</h2> <p>The <code>userAgent</code> property returns the user-agent header sent by the browser to the server:</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <div> <p id="demo"></p> <script> document.getElementById("demo").innerHTML = navigator.userAgent; </script></div> <a href="https://www.w3schools.com/js/tryit.asp?filename=tryjs_nav_userAgent" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Try it Yourself »</a> </div> <hr /> <div> <h2>Warning</h2> <p>The information from the navigator object can often be misleading.</p> <p>The navigator object should <strong>not be used to detect browser versions</strong> because:</p> <ul> <li>Different browsers can use the same name</li> <li>The navigator data can be changed by the browser owner</li> <li>Some browsers misidentify themselves to bypass site tests</li> <li>Browsers cannot report new operating systems, released later than the browser</li> </ul> </div> <hr /> <h2>The Browser Platform</h2> <p>The <code>platform</code> property returns the browser platform (operating system):</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <div> <p id="demo"></p> <script> document.getElementById("demo").innerHTML = navigator.platform; </script></div> <a href="https://www.w3schools.com/js/tryit.asp?filename=tryjs_nav_platform" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Try it Yourself »</a> </div> <hr /> <h2>The Browser Language</h2> <p>The <code>language</code> property returns the browser's language:</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <div> <p id="demo"></p> <script> document.getElementById("demo").innerHTML = navigator.language; </script></div> <a href="https://www.w3schools.com/js/tryit.asp?filename=tryjs_nav_language" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Try it Yourself »</a> </div> <hr /> <h2>Is The Browser Online?</h2> <p>The <code>onLine</code> property returns true if the browser is online:</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <div> <p id="demo"></p> <script> document.getElementById("demo").innerHTML = navigator.onLine; </script></div> <a href="https://www.w3schools.com/js/tryit.asp?filename=tryjs_nav_online" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Try it Yourself »</a> </div> <hr /> <h2>Is Java Enabled?</h2> <p>The <code>javaEnabled()</code> method returns true if <a href="https://www.w3schools.com/java/default.asp">Java</a> is enabled:</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <div> <p id="demo"></p> <script> document.getElementById("demo").innerHTML = navigator.javaEnabled(); </script></div> </div> <h1>JavaScript Popup Boxes</h1> <p>JavaScript has three kind of popup boxes: Alert box, Confirm box, and Prompt box.</p> <hr /> <h2>Alert Box</h2> <p>An alert box is often used if you want to make sure information comes through to the user.</p> <p>When an alert box pops up, the user will have to click "OK" to proceed.</p> <h3>Syntax</h3> <div> <div>window.alert("<em>sometext</em>");</div> </div> <p>The <code>window.alert()</code> method can be written without the window prefix.</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <div>alert("I am an alert box!");</div> <a href="https://www.w3schools.com/js/tryit.asp?filename=tryjs_alert" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Try it Yourself »</a> </div> <hr /> <h2>Confirm Box</h2> <p>A confirm box is often used if you want the user to verify or accept something.</p> <p>When a confirm box pops up, the user will have to click either "OK" or "Cancel" to proceed.</p> <p>If the user clicks "OK", the box returns <strong>true</strong>. If the user clicks "Cancel", the box returns <strong>false</strong>.</p> <h3>Syntax</h3> <div> <div>window.confirm("<em>sometext</em>");</div> </div> <p>The <code>window.confirm()</code> method can be written without the window prefix.</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <div>if (confirm("Press a button!")) { txt = "You pressed OK!"; } else { txt = "You pressed Cancel!"; }</div> <a href="https://www.w3schools.com/js/tryit.asp?filename=tryjs_confirm" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Try it Yourself »</a> </div> <hr /> <hr /> <h2>Prompt Box</h2> <p>A prompt box is often used if you want the user to input a value before entering a page.</p> <p>When a prompt box pops up, the user will have to click either "OK" or "Cancel" to proceed after entering an input value.</p> <p>If the user clicks "OK" the box returns the input value. If the user clicks "Cancel" the box returns null.</p> <h3>Syntax</h3> <div> <div>window.prompt("<em>sometext</em>","<em>defaultText</em>");</div> </div> <p>The <code>window.prompt()</code> method can be written without the window prefix.</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <div>let person = prompt("Please enter your name", "Harry Potter"); let text; if (person == null || person == "") { text = "User cancelled the prompt."; } else { text = "Hello " + person + "! How are you today?"; }</div> <a href="https://www.w3schools.com/js/tryit.asp?filename=tryjs_prompt" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Try it Yourself »</a> </div> <hr /> <h2>Line Breaks</h2> <p>To display line breaks inside a popup box, use a back-slash followed by the character n.</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <div>alert("Hello\nHow are you?");</div> </div> <h1>JavaScript Timing Events</h1> <h2>Timing Events</h2> <p>The <code>window</code> object allows execution of code at specified time intervals. </p> <p>These time intervals are called timing events.</p> <p>The two key methods to use with JavaScript are:</p> <ul> <ul> <li><code>setTimeout(<em>function, milliseconds</em></code>) Executes a function, after waiting a specified number of milliseconds.</li> </ul> </ul> <ul> <li><code>setInterval(<em>function, milliseconds</em></code>) Same as setTimeout(), but repeats the execution of the function continuously.</li> </ul> <div> <p>The <code>setTimeout()</code> and <code>setInterval()</code> are both methods of the HTML DOM Window object.</p> </div> <hr /> <h2>The setTimeout() Method</h2> <div> <div>window.setTimeout(<em>function</em>,<em> milliseconds</em>);</div> </div> <p>The <code>window.setTimeout()</code> method can be written without the window prefix. </p> <p>The first parameter is a function to be executed.</p> <p>The second parameter indicates the number of milliseconds before execution.</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <p>Click a button. Wait 3 seconds, and the page will alert "Hello":</p> <div><button onclick="setTimeout(myFunction, 3000)">Try it</button> <script> function myFunction() { alert('Hello'); } </script></div> <a href="https://www.w3schools.com/js/tryit.asp?filename=tryjs_timing1" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Try it Yourself »</a> </div> <hr /> <hr /> <h2>How to Stop the Execution?</h2> <p>The <code>clearTimeout()</code> method stops the execution of the function specified in setTimeout().</p> <div> <div>window.clearTimeout(<em>timeoutVariable</em>)</div> </div> <p>The <code>window.clearTimeout()</code> method can be written without the window prefix. </p> <p>The <code>clearTimeout()</code> method uses the variable returned from <code>setTimeout()</code>:</p> <div> <div>myVar = setTimeout(<em>function</em>,<em> milliseconds</em>); clearTimeout(myVar);</div> </div> <p>If the function has not already been executed, you can stop the execution by calling the <code>clearTimeout()</code> method:</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <p>Same example as above, but with an added "Stop" button:</p> <div><button onclick="myVar = setTimeout(myFunction, 3000)">Try it</button> <button onclick="clearTimeout(myVar)">Stop it</button></div> <a href="https://www.w3schools.com/js/tryit.asp?filename=tryjs_settimeout2" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Try it Yourself »</a> </div> <hr /> <h2>The setInterval() Method</h2> <p>The <code>setInterval()</code> method repeats a given function at every given time-interval.</p> <div> <div>window.setInterval(<em>function</em>,<em> milliseconds</em>);</div> </div> <p>The <code>window.setInterval()</code> method can be written without the window prefix. </p> <p>The first parameter is the function to be executed.</p> <p>The second parameter indicates the length of the time-interval between each execution.</p> <p>This example executes a function called "myTimer" once every second (like a digital watch).</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <p>Display the current time:</p> <div>setInterval(myTimer, 1000); function myTimer() { const d = new Date(); document.getElementById("demo").innerHTML = d.toLocaleTimeString(); }</div> <a href="https://www.w3schools.com/js/tryit.asp?filename=tryjs_setinterval2" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Try it Yourself »</a> </div> <div> <p>There are 1000 milliseconds in one second.</p> </div> <hr /> <h2>How to Stop the Execution?</h2> <p>The <code>clearInterval()</code> method stops the executions of the function specified in the setInterval() method.</p> <div> <div>window.clearInterval(<em>timerVariable</em>)</div> </div> <p>The <code>window.clearInterval()</code> method can be written without the window prefix.</p> <p>The <code>clearInterval()</code> method uses the variable returned from <code>setInterval()</code>:</p> <div> <div>let myVar = setInterval(<em>function</em>,<em> milliseconds</em>); clearInterval(myVar);</div> </div> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <p>Same example as above, but we have added a "Stop time" button:</p> <div> <p id="demo"></p> <button onclick="clearInterval(myVar)">Stop time</button> <script> let myVar = setInterval(myTimer, 1000); function myTimer() { const d = new Date(); document.getElementById("demo").innerHTML = d.toLocaleTimeString(); } </script></div> </div> <h1>JavaScript Cookies</h1> <p>Cookies let you store user information in web pages.</p> <hr /> <h2>What are Cookies?</h2> <p>Cookies are data, stored in small text files, on your computer.</p> <p>When a web server has sent a web page to a browser, the connection is shut down, and the server forgets everything about the user.</p> <p>Cookies were invented to solve the problem "how to remember information about the user":</p> <ul> <li>When a user visits a web page, his/her name can be stored in a cookie.</li> <li>Next time the user visits the page, the cookie "remembers" his/her name.</li> </ul> <p>Cookies are saved in name-value pairs like:</p> <div> <div>username = John Doe</div> </div> <p>When a browser requests a web page from a server, cookies belonging to the page are added to the request. This way the server gets the necessary data to "remember" information about users.</p> <div> <p>None of the examples below will work if your browser has local cookies support turned off. </p> </div> <hr /> <h2>Create a Cookie with JavaScript</h2> <p>JavaScript can create, read, and delete cookies with the <code>document.cookie</code> property.</p> <p>With JavaScript, a cookie can be created like this:</p> <div> <div>document.cookie = "username=John Doe";</div> </div> <p>You can also add an expiry date (in UTC time). By default, the cookie is deleted when the browser is closed:</p> <div> <div>document.cookie = "username=John Doe; expires=Thu, 18 Dec 2013 12:00:00 UTC"; </div> </div> <p>With a path parameter, you can tell the browser what path the cookie belongs to. By default, the cookie belongs to the current page.</p> <div> <div>document.cookie = "username=John Doe; expires=Thu, 18 Dec 2013 12:00:00 UTC; path=/";</div> </div> <hr /> <hr /> <h2>Read a Cookie with JavaScript</h2> <p>With JavaScript, cookies can be read like this:</p> <div> <div>let x = document.cookie;</div> </div> <div> <p><code>document.cookie</code> will return all cookies in one string much like: cookie1=value; cookie2=value; cookie3=value;</p> </div> <hr /> <h2>Change a Cookie with JavaScript</h2> <p>With JavaScript, you can change a cookie the same way as you create it:</p> <div> <div>document.cookie = "username=John Smith; expires=Thu, 18 Dec 2013 12:00:00 UTC; path=/";</div> </div> <p>The old cookie is overwritten.</p> <hr /> <h2>Delete a Cookie with JavaScript</h2> <p>Deleting a cookie is very simple.</p> <p>You don't have to specify a cookie value when you delete a cookie.</p> <p>Just set the expires parameter to a past date:</p> <div> <div>document.cookie = "username=; expires=Thu, 01 Jan 1970 00:00:00 UTC; path=/;"; </div> </div> <div> <p>You should define the cookie path to ensure that you delete the right cookie.</p> <p>Some browsers will not let you delete a cookie if you don't specify the path.</p> </div> <hr /> <h2>The Cookie String</h2> <p>The <code>document.cookie</code> property looks like a normal text string. But it is not.</p> <p>Even if you write a whole cookie string to document.cookie, when you read it out again, you can only see the name-value pair of it.</p> <p>If you set a new cookie, older cookies are not overwritten. The new cookie is added to document.cookie, so if you read document.cookie again you will get something like:</p> <p>cookie1 = value; cookie2 = value;</p> <p><button type="button">Display All Cookies</button> <button type="button">Create Cookie 1</button> <button type="button">Create Cookie 2</button> <button type="button">Delete Cookie 1</button> <button type="button">Delete Cookie 2</button> </p> <p>If you want to find the value of one specified cookie, you must write a JavaScript function that searches for the cookie value in the cookie string.</p> <hr /> <h2>JavaScript Cookie Example</h2> <p>In the example to follow, we will create a cookie that stores the name of a visitor.</p> <p>The first time a visitor arrives to the web page, he/she will be asked to fill in his/her name. The name is then stored in a cookie.</p> <p>The next time the visitor arrives at the same page, he/she will get a welcome message.</p> <p>For the example we will create 3 JavaScript functions:</p> <ol> <li>A function to set a cookie value</li> <li>A function to get a cookie value</li> <li>A function to check a cookie value</li> </ol> <hr /> <h2>A Function to Set a Cookie</h2> <p>First, we create a <code>function</code> that stores the name of the visitor in a cookie variable:</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <div>function setCookie(cname, cvalue, exdays) { const d = new Date(); d.setTime(d.getTime() + (exdays*24*60*60*1000)); let expires = "expires="+ d.toUTCString(); document.cookie = cname + "=" + cvalue + ";" + expires + ";path=/"; }</div> </div> <p><strong>Example explained:</strong></p> <p>The parameters of the function above are the name of the cookie (cname), the value of the cookie (cvalue), and the number of days until the cookie should expire (exdays).</p> <p>The function sets a cookie by adding together the cookiename, the cookie value, and the expires string.</p> <hr /> <h2>A Function to Get a Cookie</h2> <p>Then, we create a <code>function</code> that returns the value of a specified cookie: </p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <div> <script> function getCookie(cname) { let name = cname + "="; let decodedCookie = decodeURIComponent(document.cookie); let ca = decodedCookie.split(';'); for(let i = 0; i <ca.length; i++) { let c = ca[i]; while (c.charAt(0) == ' ') { c = c.substring(1); } if (c.indexOf(name) == 0) { return c.substring(name.length, c.length); } } return ""; } </script> </div> </div> <p><strong>Function explained:</strong></p> <p>Take the cookiename as parameter (cname).</p> <p>Create a variable (name) with the text to search for (cname + "=").</p> <p>Decode the cookie string, to handle cookies with special characters, e.g. '$'</p> <p>Split document.cookie on semicolons into an array called ca (ca = decodedCookie.split(';')).</p> <p>Loop through the ca array (i = 0; i < ca.length; i++), and read out each value c = ca[i]).</p> <p>If the cookie is found (c.indexOf(name) == 0), return the value of the cookie (c.substring(name.length, c.length).</p> <p>If the cookie is not found, return "".</p> <hr /> <h2>A Function to Check a Cookie</h2> <p>Last, we create the function that checks if a cookie is set.</p> <p>If the cookie is set it will display a greeting.</p> <p>If the cookie is not set, it will display a prompt box, asking for the name of the user, and stores the username cookie for 365 days, by calling the <code>setCookie</code> function:</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <div>function checkCookie() { let username = getCookie("username"); if (username != "") { alert("Welcome again " + username); } else { username = prompt("Please enter your name:", ""); if (username != "" && username != null) { setCookie("username", username, 365); } } }</div> </div> <hr /> <h2>All Together Now</h2> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <div>function setCookie(cname, cvalue, exdays) { const d = new Date(); d.setTime(d.getTime() + (exdays * 24 * 60 * 60 * 1000)); let expires = "expires="+d.toUTCString(); document.cookie = cname + "=" + cvalue + ";" + expires + ";path=/"; } function getCookie(cname) { let name = cname + "="; let ca = document.cookie.split(';'); for(let i = 0; i < ca.length; i++) { let c = ca[i]; while (c.charAt(0) == ' ') { c = c.substring(1); } if (c.indexOf(name) == 0) { return c.substring(name.length, c.length); } } return ""; } function checkCookie() { let user = getCookie("username"); if (user != "") { alert("Welcome again " + user); } else { user = prompt("Please enter your name:", ""); if (user != "" && user != null) { setCookie("username", user, 365); } } }</div> <a href="https://www.w3schools.com/js/tryit.asp?filename=tryjs_cookie_username" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Try it Yourself »</a> </div> <p>The example above runs the <code>checkCookie()</code> function when the page loads.</p> <h1>Web APIs - Introduction</h1> <div> <p>A Web API is a developer's dream.</p> <ul> <li>It can extend the functionality of the browser</li> <li>It can greatly simplify complex functions</li> <li>It can provide easy syntax to complex code</li> </ul> </div> <h2>What is Web API?</h2> <p>API stands for <strong>A</strong>pplication <strong>P</strong>rogramming <strong>I</strong>nterface. </p> <p>A Web API is an application programming interface for the Web.</p> <p>A Browser API can extend the functionality of a web browser.</p> <p>A Server API can extend the functionality of a web server.</p> <hr /> <h2>Browser APIs</h2> <p>All browsers have a set of built-in Web APIs to support complex operations, and to help accessing data.</p> <p>For example, the Geolocation API can return the coordinates of where the browser is located.</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <p>Get the latitude and longitude of the user's position:</p> <div>const myElement = document.getElementById("demo"); function getLocation() { if (navigator.geolocation) { navigator.geolocation.getCurrentPosition(showPosition); } else { myElement.innerHTML = "Geolocation is not supported by this browser."; } } function showPosition(position) { myElement.innerHTML = "Latitude: " + position.coords.latitude + "<br>Longitude: " + position.coords.longitude; }</div> <a href="https://www.w3schools.com/js/tryit.asp?filename=tryjs_api_geo_coordinates" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Try it Yourself »</a> </div> <hr /> <hr /> <h2>Third Party APIs</h2> <p>Third party APIs are not built into your browser.</p> <p>To use these APIs, you will have to download the code from the Web.</p> <p>Examples:</p> <ul> <li>YouTube API - Allows you to display videos on a web site.</li> <li>Twitter API - Allows you to display Tweets on a web site.</li> <li>Facebook API - Allows you to display Facebook info on a web site.</li> </ul> <h1>JavaScript Validation API</h1> <h2>Constraint Validation DOM Methods</h2> <table> <tbody> <tr> <th>Property</th> <th>Description</th> </tr> <tr> <td>checkValidity()</td> <td>Returns true if an input element contains valid data.</td> </tr> <tr> <td>setCustomValidity()</td> <td>Sets the validationMessage property of an input element.</td> </tr> </tbody> </table> <hr /> <p>If an input field contains invalid data, display a message:</p> <div> <h3>The checkValidity() Method</h3> <div> <input id="id1" type="number" min="100" max="300" required> <button onclick="myFunction()">OK</button> <p id="demo"></p> <script> function myFunction() { const inpObj = document.getElementById("id1"); if (!inpObj.checkValidity()) { document.getElementById("demo").innerHTML = inpObj.validationMessage; } } </script></div> <a href="https://www.w3schools.com/js/tryit.asp?filename=tryjs_validation_check" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Try it Yourself »</a> </div> <hr /> <h2>Constraint Validation DOM Properties</h2> <table> <tbody> <tr> <th>Property</th> <th>Description</th> </tr> <tr> <td>validity</td> <td>Contains boolean properties related to the validity of an input element.</td> </tr> <tr> <td>validationMessage</td> <td>Contains the message a browser will display when the validity is false.</td> </tr> <tr> <td>willValidate</td> <td>Indicates if an input element will be validated.</td> </tr> </tbody> </table> <hr /> <hr /> <h2>Validity Properties</h2> <p>The <strong>validity property</strong> of an input element contains a number of properties related to the validity of data:</p> <table> <tbody> <tr> <th>Property</th> <th>Description</th> </tr> <tr> <td>customError</td> <td>Set to true, if a custom validity message is set.</td> </tr> <tr> <td>patternMismatch</td> <td>Set to true, if an element's value does not match its pattern attribute.</td> </tr> <tr> <td>rangeOverflow</td> <td>Set to true, if an element's value is greater than its max attribute.</td> </tr> <tr> <td>rangeUnderflow</td> <td>Set to true, if an element's value is less than its min attribute.</td> </tr> <tr> <td>stepMismatch</td> <td>Set to true, if an element's value is invalid per its step attribute.</td> </tr> <tr> <td>tooLong</td> <td>Set to true, if an element's value exceeds its maxLength attribute.</td> </tr> <tr> <td>typeMismatch</td> <td>Set to true, if an element's value is invalid per its type attribute.</td> </tr> <tr> <td>valueMissing</td> <td>Set to true, if an element (with a required attribute) has no value.</td> </tr> <tr> <td>valid</td> <td>Set to true, if an element's value is valid.</td> </tr> </tbody> </table> <hr /> <h2>Examples</h2> <p>If the number in an input field is greater than 100 (the input's <code>max</code> attribute), display a message:</p> <div> <h3>The rangeOverflow Property</h3> <div> <input id="id1" type="number" max="100"> <button onclick="myFunction()">OK</button> <p id="demo"></p> <script> function myFunction() { let text = "Value OK"; if (document.getElementById("id1").validity.rangeOverflow) { text = "Value too large"; } } </script></div> <a href="https://www.w3schools.com/js/tryit.asp?filename=tryjs_validation_rangeOverflow" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Try it Yourself »</a> </div> <p>If the number in an input field is less than 100 (the input's <code>min</code> attribute), display a message:</p> <div> <h3>The rangeUnderflow Property</h3> <div> <input id="id1" type="number" min="100"> <button onclick="myFunction()">OK</button> <p id="demo"></p> <script> function myFunction() { let text = "Value OK"; if (document.getElementById("id1").validity.rangeUnderflow) { text = "Value too small"; } } </script></div> </div> <h1>Web History API</h1> <div> <p>The Web History API provides easy methods to access the windows.history object.</p> <p>The window.history object contains the URLs (Web Sites) visited by the user.</p> </div> <hr /> <h2>The History back() Method</h2> <p>The back() method loads the previous URL in the windows.history list.</p> <p>It is the same as clicking the "back arrow" in your browser.</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <div><button onclick="myFunction()">Go Back</button> <script> function myFunction() { window.history.back(); } </script></div> </div> <p><button>Go Back</button></p> <hr /> <hr /> <h2>The History go() Method</h2> <p>The go() method loads a specific URL from the history list:</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <div><button onclick="myFunction()">Go Back 2 Pages</button> <script> function myFunction() { window.history.go(-2); } </script></div> </div> <p><button>Go Back 2 Pages</button></p> <hr /> <h2>History Object Properties</h2> <table> <tbody> <tr> <th>Property</th> <th>Description</th> </tr> <tr> <td><a href="https://www.w3schools.com/jsref/prop_his_length.asp">length</a></td> <td>Returns the number of URLs in the history list</td> </tr> </tbody> </table> <h2>History Object Methods</h2> <table> <tbody> <tr> <th>Method</th> <th>Description</th> </tr> <tr> <td><a href="https://www.w3schools.com/jsref/met_his_back.asp">back()</a></td> <td>Loads the previous URL in the history list</td> </tr> <tr> <td><a href="https://www.w3schools.com/jsref/met_his_forward.asp">forward()</a></td> <td>Loads the next URL in the history list</td> </tr> <tr> <td><a href="https://www.w3schools.com/jsref/met_his_go.asp">go()</a></td> <td>Loads a specific URL from the history list</td> </tr> </tbody> </table> <h1>Web Storage API</h1> <p>The Web Storage API is a simple syntax for storing and retrieving data in the browser. It is very easy to use:</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <div>localStorage.setItem("name", "John Doe"); localStorage.getItem("name");</div> <a href="https://www.w3schools.com/js/tryit.asp?filename=tryjs_api_storage_example" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Try it Yourself »</a> </div> <p>The Web Storage API is supported in all browsers:</p> <table> <tbody> <tr> <td>Chrome</td> <td>IE/Edge</td> <td>Firefox</td> <td>Safari</td> <td>Opera</td> </tr> <tr> <td>Yes</td> <td>Yes</td> <td>Yes</td> <td>Yes</td> <td>Yes</td> </tr> </tbody> </table> <hr /> <h2>The localStorage Object</h2> <p>The localStorage object provides access to a local storage for a particular Web Site. It allows you to store, read, add, modify, and delete data items for that domain.</p> <p>The data is stored with no expiration date, and will not be deleted when the browser is closed. </p> <p>The data will be available for days, weeks, and years.</p> <hr /> <h2>The setItem() Method</h2> <p>The localStorage.setItem() method stores a data item in a storage.</p> <p>It takes a name and a value as parameters:</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <div>localStorage.setItem("name", "John Doe");</div> </div> <hr /> <h2>The getItem() Method</h2> <p>The localStorage.getItem() method retrieves a data item from the storage.</p> <p>It takes a name as parameter:</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <div>localStorage.getItem("name");</div> </div> <hr /> <hr /> <h2>The sessionStorage Object</h2> <p>The sessionStorage object is identical to the localStorage object.</p> <p>The difference is that the sessionStorage object stores data for one session.</p> <p>The data is deleted when the browser is closed.</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <div>sessionStorage.getItem("name");</div> <a href="https://www.w3schools.com/js/tryit.asp?filename=tryjs_api_storage_example2" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Try it Yourself »</a> </div> <hr /> <h2>The setItem() Method</h2> <p>The sessionStorage.setItem() method stores a data item in a storage.</p> <p>It takes a name and a value as parameters:</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <div>sessionStorage.setItem("name", "John Doe");</div> </div> <hr /> <h2>The getItem() Method</h2> <p>The sessionStorage.getItem() method retrieves a data item from the storage.</p> <p>It takes a name as parameter:</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <div>sessionStorage.getItem("name");</div> </div> <hr /> <h2>Storage Object Properties and Methods</h2> <table> <tbody> <tr> <th>Property/Method</th> <th>Description</th> </tr> <tr> <td><a href="https://www.w3schools.com/jsref/met_storage_key.asp">key(<em>n</em>)</a> </td> <td>Returns the name of the <em>n</em>th key in the storage</td> </tr> <tr> <td><a href="https://www.w3schools.com/jsref/prop_storage_length.asp">length</a></td> <td>Returns the number of data items stored in the Storage object</td> </tr> <tr> <td><a href="https://www.w3schools.com/jsref/met_storage_getitem.asp">getItem(<em>keyname</em>)</a> </td> <td>Returns the value of the specified key name</td> </tr> <tr> <td><a href="https://www.w3schools.com/jsref/met_storage_setitem.asp">setItem(<em>keyname</em>, <em>value</em>)</a> </td> <td>Adds a key to the storage, or updates a key value (if it already exists)</td> </tr> <tr> <td><a href="https://www.w3schools.com/jsref/met_storage_removeitem.asp">removeItem(<em>keyname</em>)</a> </td> <td>Removes that key from the storage</td> </tr> <tr> <td><a href="https://www.w3schools.com/jsref/met_storage_clear.asp">clear()</a></td> <td>Empty all key out of the storage</td> </tr> </tbody> </table> <h2>Related Pages for Web Storage API</h2> <table> <tbody> <tr> <th>Property</th> <th>Description</th> </tr> <tr> <td><a href="https://www.w3schools.com/jsref/prop_win_localstorage.asp">window.localStorage</a> </td> <td>Allows to save key/value pairs in a web browser. Stores the data with no expiration date</td> </tr> <tr> <td><a href="https://www.w3schools.com/jsref/prop_win_sessionstorage.asp">window.sessionStorage</a> </td> <td>Allows to save key/value pairs in a web browser. Stores the data for one session </td> </tr> </tbody> </table> <h1>Web Workers API</h1> <p>A web worker is a JavaScript running in the background, without affecting the performance of the page.</p> <hr /> <h2>What is a Web Worker?</h2> <p>When executing scripts in an HTML page, the page becomes unresponsive until the script is finished.</p> <p>A web worker is a JavaScript that runs in the background, independently of other scripts, without affecting the performance of the page. You can continue to do whatever you want: clicking, selecting things, etc., while the web worker runs in the background.</p> <h2>Browser Support</h2> <p>The numbers in the table specify the first browser versions that fully support Web Workers:</p> <table> <tbody> <tr> <td>Chrome 4</td> <td>IE 10</td> <td>Firefox 3.5</td> <td>Safari 4</td> <td>Opera 11.5</td> </tr> <tr> <td>Jan 2010</td> <td>Sep 2012</td> <td>Jun 2009</td> <td>Jun 2009</td> <td>Jun 2011</td> </tr> </tbody> </table> <hr /> <h2>Web Workers Example</h2> <p>The example below creates a simple web worker that count numbers in the background:</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <div>Count numbers:<output></output> <p><button>Start Worker</button> <button>Stop Worker</button></p> </div> <a href="https://www.w3schools.com/js/tryit.asp?filename=tryjs_webworker" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Try it Yourself »</a> </div> <hr /> <h2>Check Web Worker Support</h2> <p>Before creating a web worker, check whether the user's browser supports it:</p> <div> <div>if (typeof(Worker) !== "undefined") { // Yes! Web worker support! // <em>Some code.....</em> } else { // Sorry! No Web Worker support.. }</div> </div> <hr /> <hr /> <h2>Create a Web Worker File</h2> <p>Now, let's create our web worker in an external JavaScript.</p> <p>Here, we create a script that counts. The script is stored in the "demo_workers.js" file:</p> <div> <div>let i = 0; function timedCount() { i ++; postMessage(i); setTimeout("timedCount()",500); } timedCount(); </div> </div> <p>The important part of the code above is the <code>postMessage()</code> method - which is used to post a message back to the HTML page.</p> <p><strong>Note:</strong> Normally web workers are not used for such simple scripts, but for more CPU intensive tasks.</p> <hr /> <h2>Create a Web Worker Object</h2> <p>Now that we have the web worker file, we need to call it from an HTML page.</p> <p>The following lines checks if the worker already exists, if not - it creates a new web worker object and runs the code in "demo_workers.js":</p> <div> <div>if (typeof(w) == "undefined") { w = new Worker("demo_workers.js"); }</div> </div> <p>Then we can send and receive messages from the web worker.</p> <p>Add an "onmessage" event listener to the web worker.</p> <div> <div> w.onmessage = function(event){ document.getElementById("result").innerHTML = event.data; }; </div> </div> <p>When the web worker posts a message, the code within the event listener is executed. The data from the web worker is stored in event.data.</p> <hr /> <h2>Terminate a Web Worker</h2> <p>When a web worker object is created, it will continue to listen for messages (even after the external script is finished) until it is terminated.</p> <p>To terminate a web worker, and free browser/computer resources, use the <code>terminate()</code> method:</p> <div> <div>w.terminate();</div> </div> <hr /> <h2>Reuse the Web Worker</h2> <p>If you set the worker variable to undefined, after it has been terminated, you can reuse the code:</p> <div> <div>w = undefined;</div> </div> <hr /> <h2>Full Web Worker Example Code</h2> <p>We have already seen the Worker code in the .js file. Below is the code for the HTML page:</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <xmp> <!DOCTYPE html> <html> <body> <p>Count numbers: <output id="result"></output></p> <button onclick="startWorker()">Start Worker</button> <button onclick="stopWorker()">Stop Worker</button> <script> let w; function startWorker() { if (typeof(w) == "undefined") { w = new Worker("demo_workers.js"); } w.onmessage = function(event) { document.getElementById("result").innerHTML = event.data; }; } function stopWorker() { w.terminate(); w = undefined; } </script> </body> </html> </xmp> <a href="https://www.w3schools.com/js/tryit.asp?filename=tryjs_webworker" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Try it Yourself »</a> </div> <hr /> <h2>Web Workers and the DOM</h2> <p>Since web workers are in external files, they do not have access to the following JavaScript objects:</p> <ul> <li>The window object</li> <li>The document object</li> <li>The parent object</li> </ul> <h1>JavaScript Fetch API</h1> <h2>A Fetch API Example</h2> <p>The example below fetches a file and displays the content:</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <div>fetch(file) .then(x => x.text()) .then(y => myDisplay(y));</div> <a href="https://www.w3schools.com/js/tryit.asp?filename=tryjs_api_fetch" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Try it Yourself »</a> </div> <p>Since Fetch is based on async and await, the example above might be easier to understand like this:</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <div>async function getText(file) { let x = await fetch(file); let y = await x.text(); myDisplay(y); }</div> <a href="https://www.w3schools.com/js/tryit.asp?filename=tryjs_api_fetch_await" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Try it Yourself »</a> </div> <p>Or even better: Use understandable names instead of x and y:</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <div>async function getText(file) { let myObject = await fetch(file); let myText = await myObject.text(); myDisplay(myText); }</div> </div> <h1>Web Geolocation API</h1> <div> <h2>Note</h2> <p>The Geolocation API will only work on secure contexts such as HTTPS.</p> <p>If your site is hosted on a non-secure origin (such as HTTP) the requests to get the users location will no longer function.</p> </div> <hr /> <h2>Using the Geolocation API</h2> <p>The <code>getCurrentPosition()</code> method is used to return the user's position.</p> <p>The example below returns the latitude and longitude of the user's position:</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <div><script> const x = document.getElementById("demo"); function getLocation() { if (navigator.geolocation) { navigator.geolocation.getCurrentPosition(showPosition); } else { x.innerHTML = "Geolocation is not supported by this browser."; } } function showPosition(position) { x.innerHTML = "Latitude: " + position.coords.latitude + "<br>Longitude: " + position.coords.longitude; } </script></div> <a href="https://www.w3schools.com/js/tryit.asp?filename=tryjs_api_geolocation" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Try it Yourself »</a> </div> <p>Example explained:</p> <ul> <li>Check if Geolocation is supported</li> <li>If supported, run the getCurrentPosition() method. If not, display a message to the user </li> <li>If the getCurrentPosition() method is successful, it returns a coordinates object to the function specified in the parameter (showPosition)</li> <li>The showPosition() function outputs the Latitude and Longitude</li> </ul> <p>The example above is a very basic Geolocation script, with no error handling.</p> <hr /> <hr /> <h2>Handling Errors and Rejections</h2> <p>The second parameter of the <code>getCurrentPosition()</code> method is used to handle errors. It specifies a function to run if it fails to get the user's location:</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <div>function showError(error) { switch(error.code) { case error.PERMISSION_DENIED: x.innerHTML = "User denied the request for Geolocation." break; case error.POSITION_UNAVAILABLE: x.innerHTML = "Location information is unavailable." break; case error.TIMEOUT: x.innerHTML = "The request to get user location timed out." break; case error.UNKNOWN_ERROR: x.innerHTML = "An unknown error occurred." break; } }</div> <a href="https://www.w3schools.com/js/tryit.asp?filename=tryjs_api_geolocation_error" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Try it Yourself »</a> </div> <hr /> <h2>Displaying the Result in a Map</h2> <p>To display the result in a map, you need access to a map service, like Google Maps.</p> <p>In the example below, the returned latitude and longitude is used to show the location in a Google Map (using a static image):</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <div>function showPosition(position) { let latlon = position.coords.latitude + "," + position.coords.longitude; let img_url = "https://maps.googleapis.com/maps/api/staticmap?center= "+latlon+"&zoom=14&size=400x300&sensor=false&key=YOUR_KEY"; document.getElementById("mapholder").innerHTML = "<img src='"+img_url+"'>"; }</div> </div> <hr /> <h2>Location-specific Information</h2> <p>This page has demonstrated how to show a user's position on a map.</p> <p>Geolocation is also very useful for location-specific information, like:</p> <ul> <li>Up-to-date local information</li> <li>Showing Points-of-interest near the user</li> <li>Turn-by-turn navigation (GPS)</li> </ul> <hr /> <h2>The getCurrentPosition() Method - Return Data</h2> <p>The <code>getCurrentPosition()</code> method returns an object on success. The latitude, longitude and accuracy properties are always returned. The other properties are returned if available:</p> <table> <tbody> <tr> <th>Property</th> <th>Returns</th> </tr> <tr> <td>coords.latitude</td> <td>The latitude as a decimal number (always returned)</td> </tr> <tr> <td>coords.longitude</td> <td>The longitude as a decimal number (always returned)</td> </tr> <tr> <td>coords.accuracy</td> <td>The accuracy of position (always returned)</td> </tr> <tr> <td>coords.altitude</td> <td>The altitude in meters above the mean sea level (returned if available)</td> </tr> <tr> <td>coords.altitudeAccuracy</td> <td>The altitude accuracy of position (returned if available)</td> </tr> <tr> <td>coords.heading</td> <td>The heading as degrees clockwise from North (returned if available)</td> </tr> <tr> <td>coords.speed</td> <td>The speed in meters per second (returned if available)</td> </tr> <tr> <td>timestamp</td> <td>The date/time of the response (returned if available)</td> </tr> </tbody> </table> <hr /> <h2>Geolocation Object - Other interesting Methods</h2> <p>The Geolocation object also has other interesting methods:</p> <ul> <li><code>watchPosition()</code> - Returns the current position of the user and continues to return updated position as the user moves (like the GPS in a car).</li> <li><code>clearWatch()</code> - Stops the <code>watchPosition()</code> method. </li> </ul> <p>The example below shows the <code>watchPosition()</code> method. You need an accurate GPS device to test this (like smartphone):</p> <div> <h5>Example</h5> <div> <script> const x = document.getElementById("demo"); function getLocation() { if (navigator.geolocation){ navigator.geolocation.watchPosition(showPosition); } else { x.innerHTML = "Geolocation is not supported by this browser."; } } function showPosition(position){ x.innerHTML = "Latitude: " + position.coords.latitude + "<br>Longitude: " + position.coords.longitude; } </script></div> </div>
